<th scope="row">Website</th>
<td><span class="official-website"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.comune.firenze.it">Official website</a></span></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Florence</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'f' in 'find'">f</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ɒ/: 'o' in 'body'">ɒ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><small title="English pronunciation respelling"><i><b>FLOR</b>-əns</i></small></a>; <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <span lang="it" xml:lang="it"><i>Firenze</i></span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Italian" title="Help:IPA/Italian">[fiˈrɛntse]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:It-Firenze.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7c/It-Firenze.ogg" class="internal" title="It-Firenze.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>)<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> is the capital city of the <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Italy" title="Regions of Italy">Italian region</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tuscany" title="Tuscany">Tuscany</a>. It is the most populous city in Tuscany, with 383,083 inhabitants in 2013, and over 1,520,000 in its metropolitan area.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Florence was a centre of <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">medieval</a> <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> trade and finance and one of the wealthiest cities of that era.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> It is considered the birthplace of the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>, and has been called "the <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> A turbulent political history includes periods of rule by the powerful <a href="/wiki/House_of_Medici" title="House of Medici">Medici</a> family and numerous religious and republican revolutions.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> From 1865 to 1871 the city was the capital of the recently established <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Kingdom of Italy</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Florentine_dialect" title="Florentine dialect">Florentine dialect</a> forms the base of <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Standard Italian</a> and it became the language of culture throughout Italy<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> due to the prestige of the masterpieces by <a href="/wiki/Dante_Alighieri" title="Dante Alighieri">Dante Alighieri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Petrarch" title="Petrarch">Petrarch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Boccaccio" title="Giovanni Boccaccio">Giovanni Boccaccio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Niccol%C3%B2_Machiavelli" title="Niccolò Machiavelli">Niccolò Machiavelli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Guicciardini" title="Francesco Guicciardini">Francesco Guicciardini</a>.</p>
<p>The city attracts millions of tourists each year, and the <a href="/wiki/Historic_Centre_of_Florence" title="Historic Centre of Florence">Historic Centre of Florence</a> was declared a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> by UNESCO in 1982. The city is noted for its culture, <a href="/wiki/Italian_Renaissance_art" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Renaissance art">Renaissance art and architecture</a> and monuments.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> The city also contains numerous museums and art galleries, such as the <a href="/wiki/Uffizi_Gallery" class="mw-redirect" title="Uffizi Gallery">Uffizi Gallery</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Pitti" title="Palazzo Pitti">Palazzo Pitti</a>, and still exerts an influence in the fields of art, culture and politics.<sup id="cite_ref-Time.com_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time.com-9">[9]</a></sup> Due to Florence's artistic and architectural heritage, it has been ranked by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> as one of the most beautiful cities in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Florence is an important city in <a href="/wiki/Italian_fashion" title="Italian fashion">Italian fashion</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Time.com_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time.com-9">[9]</a></sup> being ranked in the top 15 <a href="/wiki/Fashion_capital" title="Fashion capital">fashion capitals</a> of the world;<sup id="cite_ref-languagemonitor_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-languagemonitor-11">[11]</a></sup> furthermore, it is a major national economic centre,<sup id="cite_ref-Time.com_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Time.com-9">[9]</a></sup> as well as a tourist and industrial hub. In 2008, the city had the 17th highest average income in <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Florence" title="History of Florence">History of Florence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Florence" title="Timeline of Florence">Timeline of Florence</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Colored_woodcut_town_view_of_Florence.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Colored_woodcut_town_view_of_Florence.jpg/220px-Colored_woodcut_town_view_of_Florence.jpg" width="220" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Colored_woodcut_town_view_of_Florence.jpg/330px-Colored_woodcut_town_view_of_Florence.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Colored_woodcut_town_view_of_Florence.jpg/440px-Colored_woodcut_town_view_of_Florence.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1019" data-file-height="518" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Colored_woodcut_town_view_of_Florence.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of Florence by Hartmann Schedel, published in 1493</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Florence originated as a Roman city, and later, after a long period as a flourishing trading and banking <a href="/wiki/Medieval_commune" title="Medieval commune">medieval commune</a>, it was the birthplace of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Renaissance" title="Italian Renaissance">Italian Renaissance</a>. According to the <i><a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclopædia Britannica">Encyclopædia Britannica</a></i>, it was politically, economically, and culturally one of the most important cities in Europe and the world from the 14th to 16th centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The language spoken in the city during the 14th century was, and still is, accepted as the <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian language</a>. Almost all the writers and poets in Italian literature of the <i>golden age</i> are in some way connected with Florence, leading ultimately to the adoption of the Florentine dialect, above all the local dialects, as a literary language of choice.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Starting from the late Middle Ages, Florentine money—in the form of the gold <a href="/wiki/Florin_(Italian_coin)" title="Florin (Italian coin)">florin</a>—financed the development of industry all over Europe, from Britain to Bruges, to Lyon and Hungary. Florentine bankers financed the English kings during the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Hundred Years War">Hundred Years War</a>. They similarly financed the papacy, including the construction of their <a href="/wiki/Avignon_Papacy" title="Avignon Papacy">provisional capital of Avignon</a> and, after their return to Rome, the reconstruction and Renaissance embellishment of Rome.</p>
<p>Florence was home to the Medici, one of European history's most important noble families. <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_de%27_Medici" title="Lorenzo de' Medici">Lorenzo de' Medici</a> was considered a political and cultural mastermind of Italy in the late 15th century. Two members of the family were <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">popes</a> in the early 16th century: <a href="/wiki/Leo_X" class="mw-redirect" title="Leo X">Leo X</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clement_VII" class="mw-redirect" title="Clement VII">Clement VII</a>. <a href="/wiki/Catherine_de_Medici" class="mw-redirect" title="Catherine de Medici">Catherine de Medici</a> married king <a href="/wiki/Henry_II_of_France" title="Henry II of France">Henry II of France</a> and, after his death in 1559, reigned as regent in France. <a href="/wiki/Marie_de%27_Medici" title="Marie de' Medici">Marie de' Medici</a> married <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_France" title="Henry IV of France">Henry IV of France</a> and gave birth to the future king <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIII_of_France" title="Louis XIII of France">Louis XIII</a>. The Medici reigned as <a href="/wiki/Grand_Dukes_of_Tuscany" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Dukes of Tuscany">Grand Dukes of Tuscany</a>, starting with <a href="/wiki/Cosimo_I_de%27_Medici" class="mw-redirect" title="Cosimo I de' Medici">Cosimo I de' Medici</a> in 1569 and ending with the death of <a href="/wiki/Gian_Gastone_de%27_Medici" class="mw-redirect" title="Gian Gastone de' Medici">Gian Gastone de' Medici</a> in 1737.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_origins">Roman origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Roman origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:17em; padding: 10px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 80%; background-color: #B0C4DE;">
<div class="" style="background-color: #B0C4DE; color: black; text-align: center; font-size: larger; font-weight: bold;">Historical affiliations</div>
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div><a href="/wiki/File:Consul_et_lictores.png" class="image"><img alt="Consul et lictores.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Consul_et_lictores.png/15px-Consul_et_lictores.png" width="15" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Consul_et_lictores.png/23px-Consul_et_lictores.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Consul_et_lictores.png/30px-Consul_et_lictores.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="380" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a> 59–27 BC<br />
<p><a href="/wiki/File:Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg" class="image"><img alt="Vexilloid of the Roman Empire.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg/15px-Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg.png" width="15" height="21" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg/23px-Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg/30px-Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="245" data-file-height="343" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> 27 BC–285 AD<br />
<a href="/wiki/File:Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg" class="image"><img alt="Vexilloid of the Roman Empire.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg/15px-Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg.png" width="15" height="21" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg/23px-Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg/30px-Vexilloid_of_the_Roman_Empire.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="245" data-file-height="343" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a> 285–476<br />
<span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Odovacar_Ravenna_477.jpg/14px-Odovacar_Ravenna_477.jpg" width="14" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Odovacar_Ravenna_477.jpg/22px-Odovacar_Ravenna_477.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Odovacar_Ravenna_477.jpg/28px-Odovacar_Ravenna_477.jpg 2x" data-file-width="280" data-file-height="298" /></span> <a href="/wiki/Odoacer" title="Odoacer">Kingdom of Odoacer</a> 476–493<br />
<span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Teodorico_re_dei_Goti_%28493-526%29.png/15px-Teodorico_re_dei_Goti_%28493-526%29.png" width="15" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Teodorico_re_dei_Goti_%28493-526%29.png/23px-Teodorico_re_dei_Goti_%28493-526%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Teodorico_re_dei_Goti_%28493-526%29.png/30px-Teodorico_re_dei_Goti_%28493-526%29.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /></span> <a href="/wiki/Ostrogothic_Kingdom" title="Ostrogothic Kingdom">Ostrogothic Kingdom</a> 493–553<br />

<a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Italy.svg" class="image"><img alt="Flag of Italy.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/15px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png" width="15" height="10" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/23px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/30px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a> <a href="/wiki/Italian_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Republic">Italian Republic</a> 1946–present</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:0092_-_Wien_-_Kunsthistorisches_Museum_-_Gaius_Julius_Caesar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/0092_-_Wien_-_Kunsthistorisches_Museum_-_Gaius_Julius_Caesar.jpg/170px-0092_-_Wien_-_Kunsthistorisches_Museum_-_Gaius_Julius_Caesar.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/0092_-_Wien_-_Kunsthistorisches_Museum_-_Gaius_Julius_Caesar.jpg/255px-0092_-_Wien_-_Kunsthistorisches_Museum_-_Gaius_Julius_Caesar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/0092_-_Wien_-_Kunsthistorisches_Museum_-_Gaius_Julius_Caesar.jpg/340px-0092_-_Wien_-_Kunsthistorisches_Museum_-_Gaius_Julius_Caesar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2736" data-file-height="3648" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:0092_-_Wien_-_Kunsthistorisches_Museum_-_Gaius_Julius_Caesar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a> established Florence in 59&#160;BC</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Etruscan_civilization" title="Etruscan civilization">Etruscans</a> initially formed in 200&#160;BC the small settlement of Fiesole (Faesulae in Latin),<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> which was destroyed by <a href="/wiki/Lucius_Cornelius_Sulla" class="mw-redirect" title="Lucius Cornelius Sulla">Lucius Cornelius Sulla</a> in 80&#160;BC in reprisal for supporting the <a href="/wiki/Populares" title="Populares">populares</a> faction in Rome. The present city of Florence was established by <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a> in 59&#160;BC as a settlement for his veteran soldiers and was named originally <i>Fluentia</i>, owing to the fact that it was built between two rivers, which was later changed to <i>Florentia</i> ("flowering").<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> It was built in the style of an <a href="/wiki/Military_camp" title="Military camp">army camp</a> with the main streets, the <i><a href="/wiki/Cardo" title="Cardo">cardo</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Decumanus_Maximus" title="Decumanus Maximus">decumanus</a></i>, intersecting at the present <i><a href="/wiki/Piazza_della_Repubblica_(Florence)" class="mw-redirect" title="Piazza della Repubblica (Florence)">Piazza della Repubblica</a></i>. Situated along the <i><a href="/wiki/Via_Cassia" title="Via Cassia">Via Cassia</a></i>, the main route between Rome and the north, and within the fertile valley of the <a href="/wiki/Arno" title="Arno">Arno</a>, the settlement quickly became an important commercial centre.</p>
<p>In centuries to come, the city experienced turbulent periods of <a href="/wiki/Ostrogoths" title="Ostrogoths">Ostrogothic</a> rule, during which the city was often troubled by warfare between the <a href="/wiki/Ostrogoths" title="Ostrogoths">Ostrogoths</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantines</a>, which may have caused the population to fall to as few as 1,000 people. Peace returned under <a href="/wiki/Lombards" title="Lombards">Lombard</a> rule in the 6th century. Florence was conquered by <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a> in 774 and became part of the Duchy of Tuscany, with <a href="/wiki/Lucca" title="Lucca">Lucca</a> as capital. The population began to grow again and commerce prospered. In 854, Florence and <a href="/wiki/Fiesole" title="Fiesole">Fiesole</a> were united in one county.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_millennium">Second millennium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Second millennium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Firenze-sanminiato01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Firenze-sanminiato01.jpg/220px-Firenze-sanminiato01.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Firenze-sanminiato01.jpg/330px-Firenze-sanminiato01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Firenze-sanminiato01.jpg/440px-Firenze-sanminiato01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="681" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Firenze-sanminiato01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Basilica di <a href="/wiki/San_Miniato_al_Monte" title="San Miniato al Monte">San Miniato al Monte</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hugh,_Margrave_of_Tuscany" title="Hugh, Margrave of Tuscany">Margrave Hugo</a> chose Florence as his residency instead of <a href="/wiki/Lucca" title="Lucca">Lucca</a> at about 1000&#160;AD. The <a href="/wiki/Golden_Age" title="Golden Age">Golden Age</a> of Florentine art began around this time. In 1013, construction began on the Basilica di <a href="/wiki/San_Miniato_al_Monte" title="San Miniato al Monte">San Miniato al Monte</a>. The exterior of the church was reworked in <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque style</a> between 1059 and 1128. In 1100, Florence was a "Commune", meaning a city state. The city's primary resource was the Arno river, providing power and access for the industry (mainly textile industry), and access to the Mediterranean sea for international trade. Another great source of strength was its industrious merchant community. The Florentine merchant banking skills became recognised in Europe after they brought decisive financial innovation (e.g. bill of exchange,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> double entry book keeping) to medieval fairs. This period also saw the eclipse of Florence's formerly powerful rival <a href="/wiki/Pisa" title="Pisa">Pisa</a> (defeated by <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoa</a> in 1284 and subjugated by Florence in 1406), and the exercise of power by the <a href="/wiki/Mercantilism" title="Mercantilism">mercantile</a> elite following an anti-aristocratic movement, led by Giano della Bella, that resulted in a set of laws called the <a href="/wiki/Ordinances_of_Justice" title="Ordinances of Justice">Ordinances of Justice</a> (1293).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages_and_Renaissance">Middle Ages and Renaissance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Middle Ages and Renaissance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Florence" title="Republic of Florence">Republic of Florence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_Renaissance" title="Italian Renaissance">Italian Renaissance</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rise_of_the_Medici">Rise of the Medici</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Rise of the Medici">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leonardo_da_Vinci_statue_outside_the_Uffizi_Gallery.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Leonardo_da_Vinci_statue_outside_the_Uffizi_Gallery.jpg/170px-Leonardo_da_Vinci_statue_outside_the_Uffizi_Gallery.jpg" width="170" height="268" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Leonardo_da_Vinci_statue_outside_the_Uffizi_Gallery.jpg/255px-Leonardo_da_Vinci_statue_outside_the_Uffizi_Gallery.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Leonardo_da_Vinci_statue_outside_the_Uffizi_Gallery.jpg/340px-Leonardo_da_Vinci_statue_outside_the_Uffizi_Gallery.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="1212" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leonardo_da_Vinci_statue_outside_the_Uffizi_Gallery.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a> statue outside the <a href="/wiki/Uffizi_Gallery" class="mw-redirect" title="Uffizi Gallery">Uffizi Gallery</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Of a population estimated at 94,000 before the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a> of 1348,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> about 25,000 are said to have been supported by the city's <a href="/wiki/Wool" title="Wool">wool</a> industry: in 1345 Florence was the scene of an attempted strike by wool combers (<i>ciompi</i>), who in 1378 rose up in a brief revolt against oligarchic rule in the <a href="/wiki/Ciompi" class="mw-redirect" title="Ciompi">Revolt of the Ciompi</a>. After their suppression, Florence came under the sway (1382–1434) of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Albizzi" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Albizzi">Albizzi</a> family, who became bitter rivals of the Medici.</p>
<p>In the 15th century, Florence was among the largest cities in Europe, considered rich and economically successful. Life was not idyllic for all residents though, among whom there were great disparities in wealth.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cosimo_de%27_Medici" title="Cosimo de' Medici">Cosimo de' Medici</a> was the first Medici family member to essentially control the city from behind the scenes. Although the city was technically a democracy of sorts, his power came from a vast <a href="/wiki/Patronage" title="Patronage">patronage</a> network along with his alliance to the new immigrants, the <i>gente nuova</i> (new people). The fact that the Medici were bankers to the pope also contributed to their ascendancy. Cosimo was succeeded by his son <a href="/wiki/Piero_di_Cosimo_de%27_Medici" title="Piero di Cosimo de' Medici">Piero</a>, who was, soon after, succeeded by Cosimo's grandson, Lorenzo in 1469. Lorenzo was a great patron of the arts, commissioning works by <a href="/wiki/Michelangelo" title="Michelangelo">Michelangelo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sandro_Botticelli" title="Sandro Botticelli">Botticelli</a>. Lorenzo was an accomplished poet and musician and brought composers and singers to Florence, including <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Agricola" title="Alexander Agricola">Alexander Agricola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Ghiselin" title="Johannes Ghiselin">Johannes Ghiselin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Isaac" title="Heinrich Isaac">Heinrich Isaac</a>. By contemporary Florentines (and since), he was known as "Lorenzo the Magnificent" (Lorenzo il Magnifico).</p>
<p>Following Lorenzo de' Medici's death in 1492, he was succeeded by his son Piero&#160;II. When the French king <a href="/wiki/Charles_VIII_of_France" title="Charles VIII of France">Charles&#160;VIII</a> invaded <a href="/wiki/Northern_Italy" title="Northern Italy">northern Italy</a>, Piero&#160;II chose to resist his army. But when he realised the size of the <a href="/wiki/French_Army" title="French Army">French army</a> at the gates of Pisa, he had to accept the humiliating conditions of the French king. These made the Florentines rebel and they expelled Piero&#160;II. With his exile in 1494, the first period of Medici rule ended with the restoration of a republican government.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Savonarola_and_Machiavelli">Savonarola and Machiavelli</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Savonarola and Machiavelli">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hanging_and_burning_of_Girolamo_Savonarola_in_Florence.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Hanging_and_burning_of_Girolamo_Savonarola_in_Florence.jpg/220px-Hanging_and_burning_of_Girolamo_Savonarola_in_Florence.jpg" width="220" height="192" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Hanging_and_burning_of_Girolamo_Savonarola_in_Florence.jpg/330px-Hanging_and_burning_of_Girolamo_Savonarola_in_Florence.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Hanging_and_burning_of_Girolamo_Savonarola_in_Florence.jpg/440px-Hanging_and_burning_of_Girolamo_Savonarola_in_Florence.jpg 2x" data-file-width="881" data-file-height="768" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hanging_and_burning_of_Girolamo_Savonarola_in_Florence.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Girolamo Savonarola being burnt at the stake in 1498</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During this period, the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Order" title="Dominican Order">Dominican friar</a> <a href="/wiki/Girolamo_Savonarola" title="Girolamo Savonarola">Girolamo Savonarola</a> had become <a href="/wiki/Prior" title="Prior">prior</a> of the <a href="/wiki/San_Marco,_Florence" title="San Marco, Florence">San Marco</a> monastery in 1490. He was famed for his penitential sermons, lambasting what he viewed as widespread immorality and attachment to material riches. He blamed the exile of the Medici as the work of God, punishing them for their decadence. He seized the opportunity to carry through political reforms leading to a more democratic rule. But when Savonarola publicly accused <a href="/wiki/Pope_Alexander_VI" title="Pope Alexander VI">Pope Alexander VI</a> of corruption, he was banned from speaking in public. When he broke this ban, he was excommunicated. The Florentines, tired of his extreme teachings, turned against him and arrested him. He was convicted as a heretic and <a href="/wiki/Death_by_burning" title="Death by burning">burned at the stake</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Piazza_della_Signoria" title="Piazza della Signoria">Piazza della Signoria</a> on 23 May 1498.</p>
<p>A second individual of unusually acute insight was <a href="/wiki/Niccol%C3%B2_Machiavelli" title="Niccolò Machiavelli">Niccolò Machiavelli</a>, whose prescriptions for Florence's regeneration under strong leadership have often been seen as a legitimisation of political expediency and even malpractice. In other words, Machiavelli was a political thinker, perhaps most renowned for his political handbook, titled <a href="/wiki/The_Prince" title="The Prince">The Prince</a>, which is about ruling and the exercise of power. Commissioned by the Medici, Machiavelli also wrote the <a href="/wiki/Florentine_Histories" title="Florentine Histories">Florentine Histories</a>, the history of the city. Florentines drove out the Medici for a second time and re-established a republic on 16 May 1527. Restored twice with the support of both Emperor and Pope, the Medici in 1537 became hereditary dukes of Florence, and in 1569 <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Tuscany" title="Grand Duchy of Tuscany">Grand Dukes of Tuscany</a>, ruling for two centuries. In all Tuscany, only the Republic of Lucca (later a <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Lucca" title="Duchy of Lucca">Duchy</a>) and the Principality of <a href="/wiki/Piombino" title="Piombino">Piombino</a> were independent from Florence.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="18th_and_19th_centuries">18th and 19th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 18th and 19th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wenceslaus_Werlin-Leopold_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor_and_his_family.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Wenceslaus_Werlin-Leopold_II%2C_Holy_Roman_Emperor_and_his_family.jpg/220px-Wenceslaus_Werlin-Leopold_II%2C_Holy_Roman_Emperor_and_his_family.jpg" width="220" height="181" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Wenceslaus_Werlin-Leopold_II%2C_Holy_Roman_Emperor_and_his_family.jpg/330px-Wenceslaus_Werlin-Leopold_II%2C_Holy_Roman_Emperor_and_his_family.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Wenceslaus_Werlin-Leopold_II%2C_Holy_Roman_Emperor_and_his_family.jpg/440px-Wenceslaus_Werlin-Leopold_II%2C_Holy_Roman_Emperor_and_his_family.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2879" data-file-height="2366" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wenceslaus_Werlin-Leopold_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor_and_his_family.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Leopold_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Leopold II, Holy Roman Emperor">Leopold II, Holy Roman Emperor</a> and his family. Leopold was, from 1765 to 1790, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_duke" title="Grand duke">Grand Duke</a> of Tuscany</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The extinction of the Medici dynasty and the accession in 1737 of <a href="/wiki/Francis_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Francis I, Holy Roman Emperor">Francis Stephen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lorraine_(duchy)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lorraine (duchy)">duke of Lorraine</a> and husband of <a href="/wiki/Maria_Theresa_of_Austria" class="mw-redirect" title="Maria Theresa of Austria">Maria Theresa of Austria</a>, led to Tuscany's temporary inclusion in the territories of the Austrian crown. It became a <a href="/wiki/Secundogeniture" title="Secundogeniture">secundogeniture</a> of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lorraine" title="House of Lorraine">Habsburg-Lorraine</a> dynasty, who were deposed for the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bourbon-Parma" title="House of Bourbon-Parma">House of Bourbon-Parma</a> in 1801. From 1801 to 1807 Florence was the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleonic</a> client state <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Etruria" title="Kingdom of Etruria">Kingdom of Etruria</a>. Bourbon-Parma were deposed in December 1807 when Tuscany was annexed by <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">France</a>. Florence was the <a href="/wiki/Prefectures_in_France" title="Prefectures in France">prefecture</a> of the French département of <a href="/wiki/Arno_(department)" title="Arno (department)">Arno</a> from 1808 to the fall of <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon I">Napoleon</a> in 1814. The Habsburg-Lorraine dynasty was restored on the throne of Tuscany at the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a> but finally deposed in 1859. Tuscany became a region of the Kingdom of Italy in 1861.</p>
<p>Florence replaced <a href="/wiki/Turin" title="Turin">Turin</a> as Italy's capital in 1865 and, in an effort to modernise the city, the old market in the Piazza del Mercato Vecchio and many medieval houses were pulled down and replaced by a more formal street plan with newer houses. The Piazza (first renamed Piazza <a href="/wiki/Victor_Emmanuel_II_of_Italy" title="Victor Emmanuel II of Italy">Vittorio Emanuele&#160;II</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Piazza_della_Repubblica_(Florence)" class="mw-redirect" title="Piazza della Repubblica (Florence)">Piazza della Repubblica</a>, the present name) was significantly widened and a large triumphal arch was constructed at the west end. This development was unpopular and was prevented from continuing by the efforts of several British and American people living in the city.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A museum recording the destruction stands nearby today.</p>
<p>The country's second capital city was superseded by Rome six years later, after the withdrawal of the French troops made its addition to the kingdom possible.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SanMiniatoAlMonte-Cimetiere.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/SanMiniatoAlMonte-Cimetiere.jpg/220px-SanMiniatoAlMonte-Cimetiere.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/SanMiniatoAlMonte-Cimetiere.jpg/330px-SanMiniatoAlMonte-Cimetiere.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/SanMiniatoAlMonte-Cimetiere.jpg/440px-SanMiniatoAlMonte-Cimetiere.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2511" data-file-height="1885" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SanMiniatoAlMonte-Cimetiere.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Porte Sante</i> cemetery, burial place of notable figures of Florentine history.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After doubling during the 19th century, Florence's population was to triple in the 20th, resulting from growth in tourism, trade, <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">financial services</a> and industry.</p>
<p>During World War II the city experienced a year-long German occupation (1943–1944) and was declared an <a href="/wiki/Open_city" title="Open city">open city</a> by the retreating Germans after New Zealand troops stormed the Pian dei Cerri hills overlooking the city. The <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> soldiers who died driving the Germans from Tuscany are buried in cemeteries outside the city (Americans about nine kilometres (5.6 miles) south of the city, British and Commonwealth soldiers a few kilometres east of the centre on the right bank of the Arno). In 1944, the retreating Germans decided to demolish all the bridges along the <a href="/wiki/Arno" title="Arno">Arno</a> linking the district of Oltrarno to the rest of the city, making it difficult for the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British troops</a> to cross. However, at the last moment Charles Steinhauslin, at the time consulate of 26 countries in Florence, convinced the German general in Italy that the <a href="/wiki/Ponte_Vecchio" title="Ponte Vecchio">Ponte Vecchio</a> was not to be destroyed due to its historical value.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Instead, an equally historic area of streets directly to the south of the bridge, including part of the <a href="/wiki/Vasari_Corridor" title="Vasari Corridor">Corridoio Vasariano</a>, was destroyed using mines. Since then the bridges have been restored to their original forms using as many of the remaining materials as possible, but the buildings surrounding the Ponte Vecchio have been rebuilt in a style combining the old with modern design. Shortly before leaving Florence, as they knew that they would soon have to retreat, the Germans executed many <a href="/wiki/Freedom_fighter" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom fighter">freedom fighters</a> and political opponents publicly, in streets and squares including the Piazza Santo Spirito.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Florence was liberated by the New Zealand Army (2nd New Zealand Division) and South African troops on 4 August 1944.</p>
<p>At the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="World War II in Europe">World War II in Europe</a>, in May 1945, the US Army's Information and Educational Branch was ordered to establish an overseas university campus for demobilised American service men and women in Florence, Italy. The first American University for service personnel was established in June 1945 at the School of Aeronautics in Florence, Italy. Some 7,500 soldier-students were to pass through the University during its four one-month sessions (see <a href="/wiki/G._I._American_Universities" class="mw-redirect" title="G. I. American Universities">G. I. American Universities</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 1966, the <a href="/wiki/1966_Flood_of_the_River_Arno_in_Florence" class="mw-redirect" title="1966 Flood of the River Arno in Florence">Arno flooded</a> parts of the centre, damaging many art treasures. Around the city there are tiny placards on the walls noting where the flood waters reached at their highest point.</p>
<p><span id="sinkhole"></span> On 25 May 2016 the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> reported that a <a href="/wiki/Sinkhole" title="Sinkhole">sinkhole</a>, thought to have been caused by a bursting of a water pipe, opened up a 200-metre (660&#160;ft) hole on the <a href="/wiki/Arno_river" class="mw-redirect" title="Arno river">Arno river</a> bank in Florence.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:502px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Florence_view_from_Piazzale_Michelangelo_-_Florence,_Italy_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Florence_view_from_Piazzale_Michelangelo_-_Florence%2C_Italy_-_panoramio.jpg/500px-Florence_view_from_Piazzale_Michelangelo_-_Florence%2C_Italy_-_panoramio.jpg" width="500" height="231" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Florence_view_from_Piazzale_Michelangelo_-_Florence%2C_Italy_-_panoramio.jpg/750px-Florence_view_from_Piazzale_Michelangelo_-_Florence%2C_Italy_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Florence_view_from_Piazzale_Michelangelo_-_Florence%2C_Italy_-_panoramio.jpg/1000px-Florence_view_from_Piazzale_Michelangelo_-_Florence%2C_Italy_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2868" data-file-height="1325" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Florence_view_from_Piazzale_Michelangelo_-_Florence,_Italy_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
November 2005 view of the city and Arno valley, with the Apennine mountains in the background</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Florence lies in a basin formed by the hills of <a href="/wiki/Villa_Medici_at_Careggi" title="Villa Medici at Careggi">Careggi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fiesole" title="Fiesole">Fiesole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Settignano" title="Settignano">Settignano</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arcetri" title="Arcetri">Arcetri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poggio_Imperiale" title="Poggio Imperiale">Poggio Imperiale</a> and Bellosguardo (Florence). The Arno river, three other minor rivers (Mugnone, Ema and Greve) and some streams flow through it.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Florence_with_snow_cover_in_December_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Florence_with_snow_cover_in_December_2009.jpg/220px-Florence_with_snow_cover_in_December_2009.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Florence_with_snow_cover_in_December_2009.jpg/330px-Florence_with_snow_cover_in_December_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Florence_with_snow_cover_in_December_2009.jpg/440px-Florence_with_snow_cover_in_December_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Florence_with_snow_cover_in_December_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Florence with snow cover in December 2009</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Florence has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">humid subtropical climate</a> (<i>Cfa</i>), slightly tending to <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean</a> (<i>Csa</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> It has hot summers with moderate or light rainfall and cool, damp winters. As Florence lacks a prevailing wind, summer temperatures are higher than along the coast. Rainfall in summer is <a href="/wiki/Precipitation_types_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation types (meteorology)">convectional</a>, while relief rainfall dominates in the winter. Snow flurries happen almost every year,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> but often result in no accumulation.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The highest officially recorded temperature was 42.6&#160;°C (108.7&#160;°F) on 26 July 1983 and the lowest was −23.2&#160;°C (−9.8&#160;°F) on 12 January 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<div style="width:70%">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Florence" title="List of mayors of Florence">List of mayors of Florence</a></div>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
<div style="width: 155px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
<div style="margin:33.5px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Quartieri_storici_Firenze.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Quartieri_storici_Firenze.png/120px-Quartieri_storici_Firenze.png" width="120" height="83" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Quartieri_storici_Firenze.png/180px-Quartieri_storici_Firenze.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Quartieri_storici_Firenze.png/240px-Quartieri_storici_Firenze.png 2x" data-file-width="429" data-file-height="297" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>The traditional boroughs of the whole <i>comune</i> of Florence</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">
<div style="width: 155px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;">
<div style="margin:22.5px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Quartieri_di_Firenze.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Quartieri_di_Firenze.gif/120px-Quartieri_di_Firenze.gif" width="120" height="105" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Quartieri_di_Firenze.gif/180px-Quartieri_di_Firenze.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/81/Quartieri_di_Firenze.gif 2x" data-file-width="235" data-file-height="205" /></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p>The 5 administrative boroughs of the whole <i>comune</i> of Florence</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
</ul>
<p>The legislative body of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_communes" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian communes">municipality</a> is the City Council (<i>Consiglio Comunale</i>), which is composed of 36 councillors elected every five years with a proportional system, contextually to the mayoral elections. The executive body is the City Committee (<i>Giunta Comunale</i>), composed by 7 <a href="/wiki/Assessor_(Italy)" title="Assessor (Italy)">assessors</a>, that is nominated and presieded over by a directly elected <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Florence" title="List of mayors of Florence">Mayor</a>. The current mayor of Florence is <a href="/wiki/Dario_Nardella" title="Dario Nardella">Dario Nardella</a>.</p>
<p>The municipality of Florence is subdivided into five administrative Boroughs (<i>Quartieri</i>). Each Borough is governed by a Council (<i>Consiglio</i>) and a President, elected contextually to the city Mayor. The urban organisation is governed by the Italian Constitution (art. 114). The Boroughs have the power to advise the Mayor with nonbinding opinions on a large spectrum of topics (environment, construction, public health, local markets) and exercise the functions delegated to them by the City Council; in addition they are supplied with an autonomous founding in order to finance local activities. The Boroughs are:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Historic_Centre_of_Florence" title="Historic Centre of Florence">Centro storico</a> (Historic Centre); population: 67,170;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Campo_di_Marte" class="mw-redirect" title="Campo di Marte">Campo di Marte</a>; population: 88,588;</li>
<li>Gavinana-<a href="/wiki/Galluzzo" title="Galluzzo">Galluzzo</a>; population: 40,907;</li>
<li>Isolotto-<a href="/wiki/Legnaia" title="Legnaia">Legnaia</a>; population: 66,636;</li>
<li>Rifredi; population: 103,761.</li>
</ul>
<p>All of the five boroughs are governed by the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(Italy)" title="Democratic Party (Italy)">Democratic Party</a>.</p>
<p>The former Italian Prime Minister (2014-2016), <a href="/wiki/Matteo_Renzi" title="Matteo Renzi">Matteo Renzi</a>, served as mayor from 2009 to 2014.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_sights">Main sights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Main sights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Florence" class="mw-redirect" title="Architecture of Florence">Architecture of Florence</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Florence_Cathedral.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Florence_Cathedral.jpg/220px-Florence_Cathedral.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Florence_Cathedral.jpg/330px-Florence_Cathedral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Florence_Cathedral.jpg/440px-Florence_Cathedral.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Florence_Cathedral.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Florence Cathedral</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palazzo_Vecchio_by_nigth.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Palazzo_Vecchio_by_nigth.jpg/220px-Palazzo_Vecchio_by_nigth.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Palazzo_Vecchio_by_nigth.jpg/330px-Palazzo_Vecchio_by_nigth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Palazzo_Vecchio_by_nigth.jpg/440px-Palazzo_Vecchio_by_nigth.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4326" data-file-height="3245" /></a>
