</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1835_S.D.U.K._City_Map_or_Plan_of_Florence_or_Firenze,_Italy_-_Geographicus_-_Florence-SDUK-1835.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/1835_S.D.U.K._City_Map_or_Plan_of_Florence_or_Firenze%2C_Italy_-_Geographicus_-_Florence-SDUK-1835.jpg/220px-1835_S.D.U.K._City_Map_or_Plan_of_Florence_or_Firenze%2C_Italy_-_Geographicus_-_Florence-SDUK-1835.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/1835_S.D.U.K._City_Map_or_Plan_of_Florence_or_Firenze%2C_Italy_-_Geographicus_-_Florence-SDUK-1835.jpg/330px-1835_S.D.U.K._City_Map_or_Plan_of_Florence_or_Firenze%2C_Italy_-_Geographicus_-_Florence-SDUK-1835.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/1835_S.D.U.K._City_Map_or_Plan_of_Florence_or_Firenze%2C_Italy_-_Geographicus_-_Florence-SDUK-1835.jpg/440px-1835_S.D.U.K._City_Map_or_Plan_of_Florence_or_Firenze%2C_Italy_-_Geographicus_-_Florence-SDUK-1835.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1848" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1835_S.D.U.K._City_Map_or_Plan_of_Florence_or_Firenze,_Italy_-_Geographicus_-_Florence-SDUK-1835.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1835 City Map of Florence, still largely in the confines of its medieval city centre.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ponte_Vecchio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Ponte_Vecchio.jpg/220px-Ponte_Vecchio.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Ponte_Vecchio.jpg/330px-Ponte_Vecchio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Ponte_Vecchio.jpg/440px-Ponte_Vecchio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ponte_Vecchio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ponte_Vecchio" title="Ponte Vecchio">Ponte Vecchio</a>, which spans the <a href="/wiki/Arno_river" class="mw-redirect" title="Arno river">Arno river</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Florence is known as the "cradle of the Renaissance" (<i>la culla del Rinascimento</i>) for its monuments, churches, and buildings. The best-known site of Florence is the domed cathedral of the city, <a href="/wiki/Florence_Cathedral" title="Florence Cathedral">Santa Maria del Fiore</a>, known as <i>The Duomo</i>, whose dome was built by <a href="/wiki/Filippo_Brunelleschi" title="Filippo Brunelleschi">Filippo Brunelleschi</a>. The nearby <a href="/wiki/Campanile" class="mw-redirect" title="Campanile">Campanile</a> (partly designed by <a href="/wiki/Giotto_di_Bondone" class="mw-redirect" title="Giotto di Bondone">Giotto</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Baptistery_of_Florence_Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="Baptistery of Florence Cathedral">Baptistery</a> buildings are also highlights. The dome, 600 years after its completion, is still the largest dome built in brick and mortar in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> In 1982, the <b><a href="/wiki/Historic_Centre_of_Florence" title="Historic Centre of Florence">historic centre of Florence</a></b> (Italian: <i>centro storico di Firenze</i>) was declared a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> by the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> The centre of the city is contained in <a href="/wiki/Defensive_wall" title="Defensive wall">medieval walls</a> that were built in the 14th century to defend the city. At the heart of the city, in <a href="/wiki/Piazza_della_Signoria" title="Piazza della Signoria">Piazza della Signoria</a>, is <a href="/wiki/Bartolomeo_Ammannati" title="Bartolomeo Ammannati">Bartolomeo Ammannati</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Fountain_of_Neptune,_Florence" title="Fountain of Neptune, Florence">Fountain of Neptune</a> (1563–1565), which is a masterpiece of <a href="/wiki/Marble_sculpture" title="Marble sculpture">marble sculpture</a> at the terminus of a still functioning Roman <a href="/wiki/Aqueduct_(watercourse)" class="mw-redirect" title="Aqueduct (watercourse)">aqueduct</a>.</p>
<p>The layout and structure of Florence in many ways harkens back to the Roman era, where it was designed as a <a href="/wiki/Garrison" title="Garrison">garrison</a> settlement.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> Nevertheless, the majority of the city was built during the Renaissance.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> Despite the strong presence of Renaissance architecture within the city, traces of <a href="/wiki/Medieval_architecture" title="Medieval architecture">medieval</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">Neoclassical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Modern_architecture" title="Modern architecture">modern architecture</a> can be found. The <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Vecchio" title="Palazzo Vecchio">Palazzo Vecchio</a> as well as the Duomo, or the city's Cathedral, are the two buildings which dominate Florence's skyline.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The River Arno, which cuts through the old part of the city, is as much a character in Florentine history as many of the people who lived there. Historically, the locals have had a love-hate relationship with the Arno – which alternated between nourishing the city with commerce, and destroying it by flood.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Firenze-Florenz-Florence_at_night_from_Piazzale_Michelangelo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Firenze-Florenz-Florence_at_night_from_Piazzale_Michelangelo.jpg/220px-Firenze-Florenz-Florence_at_night_from_Piazzale_Michelangelo.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Firenze-Florenz-Florence_at_night_from_Piazzale_Michelangelo.jpg/330px-Firenze-Florenz-Florence_at_night_from_Piazzale_Michelangelo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Firenze-Florenz-Florence_at_night_from_Piazzale_Michelangelo.jpg/440px-Firenze-Florenz-Florence_at_night_from_Piazzale_Michelangelo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4374" data-file-height="2916" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Firenze-Florenz-Florence_at_night_from_Piazzale_Michelangelo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Florence at night from Piazzale Michelangelo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>One of the bridges in particular stands out — the Ponte Vecchio (<i>Old Bridge</i>), whose most striking feature is the multitude of shops built upon its edges, held up by stilts. The bridge also carries <a href="/wiki/Vasari_Corridor" title="Vasari Corridor">Vasari's elevated corridor</a> linking the Uffizi to the Medici residence (<a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Pitti" title="Palazzo Pitti">Palazzo Pitti</a>). Although the original bridge was constructed by the <a href="/wiki/Etruscan_civilization" title="Etruscan civilization">Etruscans</a>, the current bridge was rebuilt in the 14th century. It is the only bridge in the city to have survived World War&#160;II intact. It is the first example in the western world of a bridge built using segmental <a href="/wiki/Arch" title="Arch">arches</a>, that is, arches less than a semicircle, to reduce both span-to-rise ratio and the numbers of pillars to allow lesser encumbrance in the riverbed (being in this much more successful than the Roman <a href="/wiki/Alcon%C3%A9tar_Bridge" title="Alconétar Bridge">Alconétar Bridge</a>).</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vechio_Ponte_Santa_Trinita_with_the_Oltrarno_district.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Vechio_Ponte_Santa_Trinita_with_the_Oltrarno_district.jpg/220px-Vechio_Ponte_Santa_Trinita_with_the_Oltrarno_district.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Vechio_Ponte_Santa_Trinita_with_the_Oltrarno_district.jpg/330px-Vechio_Ponte_Santa_Trinita_with_the_Oltrarno_district.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Vechio_Ponte_Santa_Trinita_with_the_Oltrarno_district.jpg/440px-Vechio_Ponte_Santa_Trinita_with_the_Oltrarno_district.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="681" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vechio_Ponte_Santa_Trinita_with_the_Oltrarno_district.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ponte_Santa_Trinita" title="Ponte Santa Trinita">Ponte Santa Trinita</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Oltrarno" title="Oltrarno">Oltrarno</a> district</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The church of <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_San_Lorenzo,_Florence" class="mw-redirect" title="Basilica of San Lorenzo, Florence">San Lorenzo</a> contains the <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_San_Lorenzo,_Florence" class="mw-redirect" title="Basilica of San Lorenzo, Florence">Medici Chapel</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Mausoleum" title="Mausoleum">mausoleum</a> of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Medici" title="House of Medici">Medici family</a>—the most powerful family in Florence from the 15th to the 18th century. Nearby is the Uffizi Gallery, one of the finest art museums in the world – founded on a large bequest from the last member of the Medici family.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Florence_Duomo_from_Michelangelo_hill.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Florence_Duomo_from_Michelangelo_hill.jpg/220px-Florence_Duomo_from_Michelangelo_hill.jpg" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Florence_Duomo_from_Michelangelo_hill.jpg/330px-Florence_Duomo_from_Michelangelo_hill.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Florence_Duomo_from_Michelangelo_hill.jpg/440px-Florence_Duomo_from_Michelangelo_hill.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3308" data-file-height="2399" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Florence_Duomo_from_Michelangelo_hill.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Florence Duomo as seen from Michelangelo hill.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Uffizi is located at the corner of <a href="/wiki/Piazza_della_Signoria" title="Piazza della Signoria">Piazza della Signoria</a>, a site important for being the centre of Florence's civil life and government for centuries. The <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_della_Signoria" class="mw-redirect" title="Palazzo della Signoria">Palazzo della Signoria</a> facing it is still home of the municipal government. Many significant episodes in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_art" title="History of art">history of art</a> and political changes were staged here, such as:</p>
<ul>
<li>In 1301, <a href="/wiki/Dante_Alighieri" title="Dante Alighieri">Dante Alighieri</a> was sent into exile from here (commemorated by a plaque on one of the walls of the Uffizi).</li>
<li>On 26 April 1478, Jacopo de' Pazzi and his retainers tried to raise the city against the Medici after the plot known as <i>La congiura dei Pazzi</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Pazzi_conspiracy" title="Pazzi conspiracy">The Pazzi conspiracy</a></i>), murdering <a href="/wiki/Giuliano_de%27_Medici_(1453%E2%80%931478)" class="mw-redirect" title="Giuliano de' Medici (1453–1478)">Giuliano di Piero de' Medici</a> and wounding his brother Lorenzo. All the members of the plot who could be apprehended were seized by the Florentines and hanged from the windows of the palace.</li>
<li>In 1497, it was the location of the <a href="/wiki/Bonfire_of_the_Vanities" class="mw-redirect" title="Bonfire of the Vanities">Bonfire of the Vanities</a> instigated by the Dominican friar and preacher <a href="/wiki/Girolamo_Savonarola" title="Girolamo Savonarola">Girolamo Savonarola</a></li>
<li>On 23 May 1498, the same Savonarola and two followers were hanged and burnt at the stake. (A round plate in the ground marks the spot where he was hanged)</li>
<li>In 1504, <a href="/wiki/David_(Michelangelo)" title="David (Michelangelo)">Michelangelo's David</a> (now replaced by a replica, since the original was moved in 1873 to the <a href="/wiki/Galleria_dell%27Accademia" title="Galleria dell'Accademia">Galleria dell'Accademia</a>) was installed in front of the Palazzo della Signoria (also known as Palazzo Vecchio).</li>
</ul>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Loggia_dei_Lanzi" title="Loggia dei Lanzi">Loggia dei Lanzi</a> in Piazza della Signoria is the location of a number of statues by other sculptors such as <a href="/wiki/Donatello" title="Donatello">Donatello</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giambologna" title="Giambologna">Giambologna</a>, Ammannati and <a href="/wiki/Benvenuto_Cellini" title="Benvenuto Cellini">Cellini</a>, although some have been replaced with copies to preserve the originals.</p>
<h3><span id="Monuments,_museums_and_religious_buildings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Monuments.2C_museums_and_religious_buildings">Monuments, museums and religious buildings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Monuments, museums and religious buildings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_churches_in_Florence" title="List of churches in Florence">List of churches in Florence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Theatres_in_Florence" title="Theatres in Florence">Theatres in Florence</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Galeri.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Galeri.jpg/250px-Galeri.jpg" width="250" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Galeri.jpg/375px-Galeri.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Galeri.jpg/500px-Galeri.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4219" data-file-height="3164" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Galeri.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Piazzale degli Uffizi</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Florence contains several palaces and buildings from various eras. The Palazzo Vecchio is the <a href="/wiki/City_and_town_halls" class="mw-redirect" title="City and town halls">town hall</a> of Florence and also an art museum. This large <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a> <a href="/wiki/Battlement" title="Battlement">crenellated</a> fortress-palace overlooks the <a href="/wiki/Piazza_della_Signoria" title="Piazza della Signoria">Piazza della Signoria</a> with its copy of Michelangelo's David statue as well as the gallery of statues in the adjacent <a href="/wiki/Loggia_dei_Lanzi" title="Loggia dei Lanzi">Loggia dei Lanzi</a>. Originally called the <i>Palazzo della Signoria</i>, after the <a href="/wiki/Signoria_of_Florence" title="Signoria of Florence">Signoria of Florence</a>, the ruling body of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Florence" title="Republic of Florence">Republic of Florence</a>, it was also given several other names: <i>Palazzo del Popolo</i>, <i>Palazzo dei Priori</i>, and <i>Palazzo Ducale</i>, in accordance with the varying use of the palace during its long history. The building acquired its current name when the Medici duke's residence was moved across the Arno to the Palazzo Pitti. It is linked to the Uffizi and the Palazzo Pitti through the <a href="/wiki/Corridoio_Vasariano" class="mw-redirect" title="Corridoio Vasariano">Corridoio Vasariano</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Medici_Riccardi" title="Palazzo Medici Riccardi">Palazzo Medici Riccardi</a>, designed by <a href="/wiki/Michelozzo" title="Michelozzo">Michelozzo di Bartolomeo</a> for <a href="/wiki/Cosimo_de%27_Medici" title="Cosimo de' Medici">Cosimo il Vecchio</a>, of the Medici family, is another major edifice, and was built between 1445 and 1460. It was well known for its stone masonry that includes rustication and ashlar. Today it is the head office of the Metropolitan City of Florence and hosts museums and the <a href="/wiki/Biblioteca_Riccardiana" title="Biblioteca Riccardiana">Riccardiana Library</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Strozzi" title="Palazzo Strozzi">Palazzo Strozzi</a>, an example of civil architecture with its rusticated stone, was inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Medici_Riccardi" title="Palazzo Medici Riccardi">Palazzo Medici</a>, but with more harmonious proportions. Today the palace is used for international expositions like the annual antique show (founded as the Biennale dell'Antiquariato in 1959), fashion shows and other cultural and artistic events. Here also is the seat of the Istituto Nazionale del Rinascimento and the noted <a href="/wiki/Gabinetto_Vieusseux" title="Gabinetto Vieusseux">Gabinetto Vieusseux</a>, with the library and reading room.<br />
There are several other notable places, including the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Rucellai" title="Palazzo Rucellai">Palazzo Rucellai</a>, designed by Leon Battista Alberti between 1446 and 1451 and executed, at least in part, by <a href="/wiki/Bernardo_Rossellino" title="Bernardo Rossellino">Bernardo Rossellino</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Davanzati" title="Palazzo Davanzati">Palazzo Davanzati</a>, which houses the museum of the Old Florentine House; the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_delle_Assicurazioni_Generali_(Florence)" class="mw-redirect" title="Palazzo delle Assicurazioni Generali (Florence)">Palazzo delle Assicurazioni Generali</a>, designed in the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Revival_architecture" title="Renaissance Revival architecture">Neo-Renaissance</a> style in 1871; the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Spini_Feroni" title="Palazzo Spini Feroni">Palazzo Spini Feroni</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Piazza_Santa_Trinita" title="Piazza Santa Trinita">Piazza Santa Trinita</a>, a historic 13th-century private palace, owned since the 1920s by shoe-designer <a href="/wiki/Salvatore_Ferragamo" title="Salvatore Ferragamo">Salvatore Ferragamo</a>; as well as various others, including the Palazzo Borghese, the Palazzo di Bianca Cappello, the <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Antinori" title="Palazzo Antinori">Palazzo Antinori</a>, and the Royal building of Santa Maria Novella.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palazzo_Pitti_Gartenfassade_Florenz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Palazzo_Pitti_Gartenfassade_Florenz.jpg/220px-Palazzo_Pitti_Gartenfassade_Florenz.jpg" width="220" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Palazzo_Pitti_Gartenfassade_Florenz.jpg/330px-Palazzo_Pitti_Gartenfassade_Florenz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Palazzo_Pitti_Gartenfassade_Florenz.jpg/440px-Palazzo_Pitti_Gartenfassade_Florenz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3018" data-file-height="1839" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palazzo_Pitti_Gartenfassade_Florenz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Pitti" title="Palazzo Pitti">Palazzo Pitti</a> on <a href="/wiki/Boboli_Gardens" title="Boboli Gardens">Boboli Gardens</a>' side</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Florence contains numerous museums and art galleries where some of the world's most important works of art are held. The city is one of the best preserved Renaissance centres of art and architecture in the world and has a high concentration of art, architecture and culture.<sup id="cite_ref-travelguide.affordabletours.com_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-travelguide.affordabletours.com-29">[29]</a></sup> In the ranking list of the 15 most visited Italian art museums, ⅔ are represented by Florentine museums.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The Uffizi is one of these, having a very large collection of international and Florentine art. The gallery is articulated in many halls, catalogued by schools and chronological order. Engendered by the Medici family's artistic collections through the centuries, it houses works of art by various painters and artists. The <a href="/wiki/Vasari_Corridor" title="Vasari Corridor">Vasari Corridor</a> is another gallery, built connecting the Palazzo Vecchio with the Pitti Palace passing by the Uffizi and over the Ponte Vecchio. The Galleria dell'Accademia houses a Michelangelo collection, including the <a href="/wiki/David_(Michelangelo)" title="David (Michelangelo)">David</a>. It has a collection of Russian icons and works by various artists and painters. Other museums and galleries include the <a href="/wiki/Bargello" title="Bargello">Bargello</a>, which concentrates on sculpture works by artists including Donatello, <a href="/wiki/Giambologna" title="Giambologna">Giambologna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michelangelo" title="Michelangelo">Michelangelo</a>; the Palazzo Pitti, containing part of the Medici family's former private collection. In addition to the Medici collection, the palace's galleries contain many Renaissance works, including several by <a href="/wiki/Raphael" title="Raphael">Raphael</a> and <a href="/wiki/Titian" title="Titian">Titian</a>, large collections of costumes, ceremonial carriages, silver, porcelain and a <a href="/wiki/Palazzo_Pitti#Gallery_of_Modern_Art" title="Palazzo Pitti">gallery of modern art</a> dating from the 18th century. Adjoining the palace are the <a href="/wiki/Boboli_Gardens" title="Boboli Gardens">Boboli Gardens</a>, elaborately landscaped and with numerous sculptures.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Il_Duomo_di_Firenze.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Il_Duomo_di_Firenze.JPG/200px-Il_Duomo_di_Firenze.JPG" width="200" height="279" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Il_Duomo_di_Firenze.JPG/300px-Il_Duomo_di_Firenze.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Il_Duomo_di_Firenze.JPG/400px-Il_Duomo_di_Firenze.JPG 2x" data-file-width="441" data-file-height="615" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Il_Duomo_di_Firenze.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The façade of the Cathedral</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are several different churches and religious buildings in Florence. The cathedral is <a href="/wiki/Florence_Cathedral" title="Florence Cathedral">Santa Maria del Fiore</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Florence_Baptistry" class="mw-redirect" title="Florence Baptistry">San Giovanni Baptistery</a> located in front of the cathedral, is decorated by numerous artists, notably by <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Ghiberti" title="Lorenzo Ghiberti">Lorenzo Ghiberti</a> with the <i>Gates of Paradise</i>. Other churches in Florence include the <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Santa_Maria_Novella" class="mw-redirect" title="Basilica of Santa Maria Novella">Basilica of Santa Maria Novella</a>, located in Santa Maria Novella square (near the <a href="/wiki/Firenze_Santa_Maria_Novella_railway_station" title="Firenze Santa Maria Novella railway station">Firenze Santa Maria Novella railway station</a>) which contains works by <a href="/wiki/Masaccio" title="Masaccio">Masaccio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Uccello" title="Paolo Uccello">Paolo Uccello</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filippino_Lippi" title="Filippino Lippi">Filippino Lippi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Domenico_Ghirlandaio" title="Domenico Ghirlandaio">Domenico Ghirlandaio</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Santa_Croce,_Florence" class="mw-redirect" title="Basilica of Santa Croce, Florence">Basilica of Santa Croce</a>, the principal Franciscan church in the city, which is situated on the Piazza di Santa Croce, about 800 metres (2,600 feet) south east of the Duomo, and is the burial place of some of the most illustrious Italians, such as Michelangelo, Galileo, Machiavelli, Foscolo, Rossini, thus it is known also as the Temple of the Italian Glories (Tempio dell'Itale Glorie); the <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_San_Lorenzo,_Florence" class="mw-redirect" title="Basilica of San Lorenzo, Florence">Basilica of San Lorenzo</a>, which is one of the largest churches in the city, situated at the centre of Florence's main market district, and the burial place of all the principal members of the Medici family from Cosimo il Vecchio to Cosimo III; <a href="/wiki/Santo_Spirito,_Florence" title="Santo Spirito, Florence">Santo Spirito</a>, in the Oltrarno quarter, facing the square with the same name; <a href="/wiki/Orsanmichele" title="Orsanmichele">Orsanmichele</a>, whose building was constructed on the site of the kitchen garden of the monastery of San Michele, now demolished; <a href="/wiki/Santissima_Annunziata,_Florence" title="Santissima Annunziata, Florence">Santissima Annunziata</a>, a Roman Catholic basilica and the mother church of the <a href="/wiki/Servite_Order" title="Servite Order">Servite order</a>; <a href="/wiki/Ognissanti,_Florence" title="Ognissanti, Florence">Ognissanti</a>, which was founded by the lay order of the Umiliati, and is among the first examples of <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque architecture</a> built in the city; the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_del_Carmine,_Florence" title="Santa Maria del Carmine, Florence">Santa Maria del Carmine</a>, in the Oltrarno district of Florence, which is the location of the <a href="/wiki/Brancacci_Chapel" title="Brancacci Chapel">Brancacci Chapel</a>, housing outstanding Renaissance frescoes by <a href="/wiki/Masaccio" title="Masaccio">Masaccio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Masolino_da_Panicale" title="Masolino da Panicale">Masolino da Panicale</a>, later finished by <a href="/wiki/Filippino_Lippi" title="Filippino Lippi">Filippino Lippi</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Medici_Chapel" title="Medici Chapel">Medici Chapel</a> with statues by Michelangelo, in the <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_San_Lorenzo,_Florence" class="mw-redirect" title="Basilica of San Lorenzo, Florence">San Lorenzo</a>; as well as several others, including <a href="/wiki/Santa_Trinita" title="Santa Trinita">Santa Trinita</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Marco,_Florence" title="San Marco, Florence">San Marco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santa_Felicita,_Florence" title="Santa Felicita, Florence">Santa Felicita</a>, <a href="/wiki/Badia_Fiorentina" title="Badia Fiorentina">Badia Fiorentina</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Gaetano,_Florence" title="San Gaetano, Florence">San Gaetano</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Miniato_al_Monte" title="San Miniato al Monte">San Miniato al Monte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florence_Charterhouse" title="Florence Charterhouse">Florence Charterhouse</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_del_Carmine,_Florence" title="Santa Maria del Carmine, Florence">Santa Maria del Carmine</a>. The city additionally contains the Orthodox Russian church of Nativity, and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Synagogue_of_Florence" title="Great Synagogue of Florence">Great Synagogue of Florence</a>, built in the 19th century.</p>
<p>Florence contains various theatres and cinemas. The Odeon Cinema of the Palazzo dello Strozzino is one of the oldest cinemas in the city. Established from 1920 to 1922<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> in a wing of the Palazzo dello Strozzino, it used to be called the <i>Cinema Teatro Savoia</i> (Savoy Cinema-Theatre), yet was later called <i>Odeon</i>. The <a href="/wiki/Teatro_della_Pergola" title="Teatro della Pergola">Teatro della Pergola</a>, located in the centre of the city on the eponymous street, is an <a href="/wiki/Opera_house" title="Opera house">opera house</a> built in the 17th century. Another theatre is the <a href="/wiki/Teatro_Comunale_Florence" title="Teatro Comunale Florence">Teatro Comunale</a> (or <i>Teatro del Maggio Musicale Fiorentino</i>), originally built as the open-air amphitheatre, the <i>Politeama Fiorentino Vittorio Emanuele</i>, which was inaugurated on 17 May 1862 with a production of <a href="/wiki/Gaetano_Donizetti" title="Gaetano Donizetti">Donizetti</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Lucia_di_Lammermoor" title="Lucia di Lammermoor">Lucia di Lammermoor</a></i> and which seated 6,000 people. There are several other theatres, such as the Saloncino Castinelli, the Teatro Puccini, the Teatro Verdi, the Teatro Goldoni and the Teatro Niccolini.</p>
<h3><span id="Squares,_streets_and_parks"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Squares.2C_streets_and_parks">Squares, streets and parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Squares, streets and parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Squares_of_Florence" class="mw-redirect" title="Squares of Florence">Squares of Florence</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gilli_(Florence)_Piazza_della_Repubblica.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Gilli_%28Florence%29_Piazza_della_Repubblica.jpg/220px-Gilli_%28Florence%29_Piazza_della_Repubblica.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Gilli_%28Florence%29_Piazza_della_Repubblica.jpg/330px-Gilli_%28Florence%29_Piazza_della_Repubblica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Gilli_%28Florence%29_Piazza_della_Repubblica.jpg/440px-Gilli_%28Florence%29_Piazza_della_Repubblica.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gilli_(Florence)_Piazza_della_Repubblica.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Piazza_della_Repubblica_(Florence)" class="mw-redirect" title="Piazza della Repubblica (Florence)">Piazza della Repubblica</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Firenze_panorama_from_the_Giardino_Bardini.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Firenze_panorama_from_the_Giardino_Bardini.jpg/220px-Firenze_panorama_from_the_Giardino_Bardini.jpg" width="220" height="46" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Firenze_panorama_from_the_Giardino_Bardini.jpg/330px-Firenze_panorama_from_the_Giardino_Bardini.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Firenze_panorama_from_the_Giardino_Bardini.jpg/440px-Firenze_panorama_from_the_Giardino_Bardini.jpg 2x" data-file-width="9684" data-file-height="2005" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Firenze_panorama_from_the_Giardino_Bardini.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Panorama composite, overview of Firenze, taken from the Giardino Bardini viewpoint.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Aside from such monuments, Florence contains numerous major squares (<i>piazze</i>) and streets. The <a href="/wiki/Piazza_della_Repubblica_(Florence)" class="mw-redirect" title="Piazza della Repubblica (Florence)">Piazza della Repubblica</a> is a square in the city centre, location of the cultural cafés and bourgeois palaces. Among the square's cafés (like Caffè Gilli, Paszkowski or the Hard Rock Cafè), the <a href="/wiki/Caff%C3%A8_Giubbe_Rosse" title="Caffè Giubbe Rosse">Giubbe Rosse</a> café has long been a meeting place for artists and writers, notably those of <a href="/wiki/Futurism" title="Futurism">Futurism</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Piazza_Santa_Croce" title="Piazza Santa Croce">Piazza Santa Croce</a> is another; dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Santa_Croce,_Florence" class="mw-redirect" title="Basilica of Santa Croce, Florence">Basilica of Santa Croce</a>, it is a rectangular square in the centre of the city where the <a href="/wiki/Calcio_Fiorentino" title="Calcio Fiorentino">Calcio Fiorentino</a> is played every year. Furthermore, there is the <a href="/wiki/Piazza_Santa_Trinita" title="Piazza Santa Trinita">Piazza Santa Trinita</a>, a square near the Arno that mark the end of the <a href="/wiki/Via_de%27_Tornabuoni" title="Via de' Tornabuoni">Via de' Tornabuoni</a> street.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Replica_of_David,_Piazza_della_Signoria,_Florence.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Replica_of_David%2C_Piazza_della_Signoria%2C_Florence.jpg/220px-Replica_of_David%2C_Piazza_della_Signoria%2C_Florence.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Replica_of_David%2C_Piazza_della_Signoria%2C_Florence.jpg/330px-Replica_of_David%2C_Piazza_della_Signoria%2C_Florence.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Replica_of_David%2C_Piazza_della_Signoria%2C_Florence.jpg/440px-Replica_of_David%2C_Piazza_della_Signoria%2C_Florence.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3300" data-file-height="2200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Replica_of_David,_Piazza_della_Signoria,_Florence.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Replica of David and other statues, Piazza della Signoria</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Other squares include the Piazza San Marco, the Piazza Santa Maria Novella, the <a href="/wiki/Piazza_Beccaria" class="mw-redirect" title="Piazza Beccaria">Piazza Beccaria</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Piazza_della_Libert%C3%A0_(Florence)" class="mw-redirect" title="Piazza della Libertà (Florence)">Piazza della Libertà</a>. The centre additionally contains several streets. Such include the <a href="/wiki/Via_Camillo_Cavour" title="Via Camillo Cavour">Via Camillo Cavour</a>, one of the main roads of the northern area of the historic centre; the Via Ghibellina, one of central Florence's longest streets; the Via dei Calzaiuoli, one of the most central streets of the historic centre which links <i>Piazza del Duomo</i> to <a href="/wiki/Piazza_della_Signoria" title="Piazza della Signoria">Piazza della Signoria</a>, winding parallel to via Roma and <i>Piazza della Repubblica</i>; the <a href="/wiki/Via_de%27_Tornabuoni" title="Via de' Tornabuoni">Via de' Tornabuoni</a>, a luxurious street in the city centre that goes from Antinori square to <a href="/wiki/Ponte_Santa_Trinita" title="Ponte Santa Trinita">ponte Santa Trinita</a>, across <a href="/wiki/Piazza_Santa_Trinita" title="Piazza Santa Trinita">Piazza Santa Trinita</a>, characterised by the presence of fashion boutiques; the <a href="/wiki/Viali_di_Circonvallazione" title="Viali di Circonvallazione">Viali di Circonvallazione</a>, 6-lane <a href="/wiki/Boulevard" title="Boulevard">boulevards</a> surrounding the northern part of the historic centre; as well as others, such as Via Roma, Via degli Speziali, Via de' Cerretani, and the Viale dei Colli.</p>
<p>Florence also contains various parks and gardens. Such include the Boboli Gardens, the <a href="/wiki/Parco_delle_Cascine" title="Parco delle Cascine">Parco delle Cascine</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Giardino_Bardini" title="Giardino Bardini">Giardino Bardini</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Orto_Botanico_di_Firenze" title="Orto Botanico di Firenze">Giardino dei Semplici</a>, amongst others.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>In 1200 the city was home to 50,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-google_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-google-32">[32]</a></sup> By 1300 the population of the city proper was 120,000, with an additional 300,000 living in the <a href="/wiki/Contado" class="mw-redirect" title="Contado">Contado</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-google2_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-google2-33">[33]</a></sup> Between 1500 and 1650 the population was around 70,000.<sup id="cite_ref-google3_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-google3-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-google4_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-google4-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 31 October 2010<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the population of the city proper is 370,702, while <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a> estimates that 696,767 people live in the <a href="/wiki/Larger_Urban_Zones" class="mw-redirect" title="Larger Urban Zones">urban area</a> of Florence. The Metropolitan Area of Florence, Prato and Pistoia, constituted in 2000 over an area of roughly 4,800 square kilometres (1,853&#160;sq&#160;mi), is home to 1.5&#160;million people. Within Florence proper, 46.8% of the population was male in 2007 and 53.2% were female. Minors (children aged 18 and less) totalled 14.10 percent of the population compared to pensioners, who numbered 25.95 percent. This compares with the Italian average of 18.06 percent (minors) and 19.94 percent (pensioners). The average age of Florence resident is 49 compared to the Italian average of 42. In the five years between 2002 and 2007, the population of Florence grew by 3.22 percent, while Italy as a whole grew by 3.56 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Birth_rate" title="Birth rate">birth rate</a> of Florence is 7.66 births per 1,000 inhabitants compared to the Italian average of 9.45 births.</p>
<p>As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 87.46% of the population was Italian. An estimated 6,000 <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a> live in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The largest immigrant group came from other European countries (mostly <a href="/wiki/Romanians" title="Romanians">Romanians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">Albanians</a>): 3.52%, East Asia (mostly <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Chinese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Filipino_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Filipino people">Filipino</a>): 2.17%, the Americas: 1.41%, and North Africa (mostly <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Moroccan</a>): 0.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Tourism is, by far, the most important of all industries and most of the Florentine economy relies on the money generated by international arrivals and students studying in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> The value tourism to the city totalled some €62.5 billion in 2015 and the number of visitors had increased by 5.5% from the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-theflorentine.net_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theflorentine.net-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, Florence was listed as the second best world city by <i>Condé Nast Traveler</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Manufacturing and commerce, however, still remain highly important. Florence is also Italy's 17th richest city in terms of average workers' earnings, with the figure being €23,265 (the overall city's income is €6,531,204,473), coming after <a href="/wiki/Mantua" title="Mantua">Mantua</a>, yet surpassing <a href="/wiki/Bolzano" title="Bolzano">Bolzano</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span id="Industry,_commerce_and_services"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry.2C_commerce_and_services">Industry, commerce and services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Industry, commerce and services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Florence is a major production and commercial centre in Italy, where the Florentine industrial complexes in the suburbs produce all sorts of goods, from furniture, rubber goods, chemicals, and food.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> However, traditional and local products, such as antiques, handicrafts, glassware, leatherwork, art reproductions, jewellery, souvenirs, elaborate metal and iron-work, shoes, accessories and high fashion clothes also dominate a fair sector of Florence's economy.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup> The city's income relies partially on services and commercial and cultural interests, such as annual fairs, theatrical and lyrical productions, art exhibitions, festivals and fashion shows, such as the <a href="/wiki/Calcio_Fiorentino" title="Calcio Fiorentino">Calcio Fiorentino</a>. Heavy industry and machinery also take their part in providing an income. In Nuovo Pignone, numerous factories are still present, and small-to medium industrial businesses are dominant. The Florence-Prato-Pistoia industrial districts and areas were known as the 'Third Italy' in the 1990s, due to the exports of high-quality goods and automobile (especially the <a href="/wiki/Vespa" title="Vespa">Vespa</a>) and the prosperity and productivity of the Florentine entrepreneurs. Some of these industries even rivalled the traditional industrial districts in <a href="/wiki/Emilia%E2%80%93Romagna" class="mw-redirect" title="Emilia–Romagna">Emilia-Romagna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Veneto" title="Veneto">Veneto</a> due to high profits and productivity.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica.com_8-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica.com-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the fourth quarter of 2015, manufacturing increased by 2.4% and exports increased by 7.2%. Leading sectors included mechanical engineering, fashion, pharmaceutics, food and wine. During 2015, permanent employment contracts increased by 48.8 percent, boosted by nationwide tax break.<sup id="cite_ref-theflorentine.net_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theflorentine.net-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Florencja_Il_Porcelino_RB.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Florencja_Il_Porcelino_RB.jpg/220px-Florencja_Il_Porcelino_RB.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Florencja_Il_Porcelino_RB.jpg/330px-Florencja_Il_Porcelino_RB.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Florencja_Il_Porcelino_RB.jpg/440px-Florencja_Il_Porcelino_RB.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Florencja_Il_Porcelino_RB.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tourists flock to the <a href="/wiki/Porcellino" title="Porcellino">Fontana del Porcellino</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Tourism is the most significant industry in central Florence. From April to October, tourists outnumber local population. Tickets to the Uffizi and Accademia museums are regularly sold out and large groups regularly fill the basilicas of <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Santa_Croce,_Florence" class="mw-redirect" title="Basilica of Santa Croce, Florence">Santa Croce</a> and <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Santa_Maria_Novella" class="mw-redirect" title="Basilica of Santa Maria Novella">Santa Maria Novella</a>, both of which charge for entry. Tickets for The Uffizi and Accademia can be purchased online prior to visiting.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> In 2010, readers of <i><a href="/wiki/Travel_%2B_Leisure" title="Travel + Leisure">Travel + Leisure</a></i> magazine ranked the city as their third favourite tourist destination.<sup id="cite_ref-travelandleisure.com_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-travelandleisure.com-43">[43]</a></sup> In 2015, Condé Nast Travel readers voted Florence as the best city in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>Studies by Euromonitor International have concluded that cultural and history-oriented tourism is generating significantly increased spending throughout Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Florence is believed to have the greatest concentration of art (in proportion to its size) in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Thus, cultural tourism is particularly strong, with world-renowned museums such as the Uffizi selling over 1.93&#160;million tickets in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The city's convention centre facilities were restructured during the 1990s and host exhibitions, conferences, meetings, social forums, concerts and other events all year.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Restaurant_in_the_Piazza_del_Duomo,_Florence,_Italy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Restaurant_in_the_Piazza_del_Duomo%2C_Florence%2C_Italy.jpg/220px-Restaurant_in_the_Piazza_del_Duomo%2C_Florence%2C_Italy.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Restaurant_in_the_Piazza_del_Duomo%2C_Florence%2C_Italy.jpg/330px-Restaurant_in_the_Piazza_del_Duomo%2C_Florence%2C_Italy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Restaurant_in_the_Piazza_del_Duomo%2C_Florence%2C_Italy.jpg/440px-Restaurant_in_the_Piazza_del_Duomo%2C_Florence%2C_Italy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Restaurant_in_the_Piazza_del_Duomo,_Florence,_Italy.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tourists and restaurant in the Piazza del Duomo</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2016, Florence had 20,588 hotel rooms in 570 facilities. International visitors use 75% of the rooms; some 18% of those were from the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> In 2014, the city had 8.5 million overnight stays.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> A Euromonitor report indicates that in 2015 the city ranked as the world's 36th most visited in the world, with over 4.95&#160;million arrivals for the year.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tourism brings revenue to Florence, but it creates certain problems. The Ponte Vecchio, The San Lorenzo Market and Santa Maria Novella are plagued by pickpockets.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The province of Florence receives roughly 13 million visitors per year<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> and in peak seasons, that can lead to over crowding at popular locations.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Mayor Dario Nardella is particularly concerned about visitors who arrive on buses, stay only a few hours, spend litlle money but contribute significantly to overcrowding. "No museum visit, just a photo from the square, the bus back and then on to Venice... We don’t want tourists like that," he said.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some tourists are less than respectful of the city's cultural heritage, according to Nardella. In June 2017, he instituted a programme of spraying church steps with water to prevent tourists from using such areas as picnic spots. While he values the benefits of tourism, there has been "an increase among those who sit down on church steps, eat their food and leave rubbish strewn on them," he explained.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> To boost the sale of traditional foods, the mayor had introduced legislation (enacted in 2016) that requires restaurants to use typical Tuscan products and rejected McDonald's application to open a location in the Piazza del Duomo.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food_and_wine_production">Food and wine production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Food and wine production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fiaschi_of_basic_Chianti.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Fiaschi_of_basic_Chianti.jpg/220px-Fiaschi_of_basic_Chianti.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Fiaschi_of_basic_Chianti.jpg/330px-Fiaschi_of_basic_Chianti.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Fiaschi_of_basic_Chianti.jpg/440px-Fiaschi_of_basic_Chianti.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fiaschi_of_basic_Chianti.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Fiascos</i> of basic Chianti.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Food and wine have long been an important staple of the economy. The <a href="/wiki/Chianti" title="Chianti">Chianti</a> region is just south of the city, and its <a href="/wiki/Sangiovese" title="Sangiovese">Sangiovese</a> grapes figure prominently not only in its <a href="/wiki/Chianti" title="Chianti">Chianti Classico</a> wines but also in many of the more recently developed Supertuscan blends. Within 32&#160;km (20&#160;mi) to the west is the Carmignano area, also home to flavourful sangiovese-based reds. The celebrated Chianti Rufina district, geographically and historically separated from the main Chianti region, is also few kilometres east of Florence. More recently, the Bolgheri region (about 150&#160;km (93&#160;mi) southwest of Florence) has become celebrated for its "<a href="/wiki/Super_Tuscan" class="mw-redirect" title="Super Tuscan">Super Tuscan</a>" reds such as <a href="/wiki/Sassicaia" class="mw-redirect" title="Sassicaia">Sassicaia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ornellaia" class="mw-redirect" title="Ornellaia">Ornellaia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-OCW-bol_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OCW-bol-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Florence&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Art_in_Florence" class="mw-redirect" title="Art in Florence">Art in Florence</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Guilds_of_Florence" title="Guilds of Florence">Guilds of Florence</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sandro_Botticelli_-_La_nascita_di_Venere_-_Google_Art_Project_-_edited.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Sandro_Botticelli_-_La_nascita_di_Venere_-_Google_Art_Project_-_edited.jpg/220px-Sandro_Botticelli_-_La_nascita_di_Venere_-_Google_Art_Project_-_edited.jpg" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Sandro_Botticelli_-_La_nascita_di_Venere_-_Google_Art_Project_-_edited.jpg/330px-Sandro_Botticelli_-_La_nascita_di_Venere_-_Google_Art_Project_-_edited.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Sandro_Botticelli_-_La_nascita_di_Venere_-_Google_Art_Project_-_edited.jpg/440px-Sandro_Botticelli_-_La_nascita_di_Venere_-_Google_Art_Project_-_edited.jpg 2x" data-file-width="30000" data-file-height="18840" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sculptures_in_the_Loggia_dei_Lanzi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Sculptures_in_the_Loggia_dei_Lanzi.jpg/220px-Sculptures_in_the_Loggia_dei_Lanzi.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Sculptures_in_the_Loggia_dei_Lanzi.jpg/330px-Sculptures_in_the_Loggia_dei_Lanzi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Sculptures_in_the_Loggia_dei_Lanzi.jpg/440px-Sculptures_in_the_Loggia_dei_Lanzi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>
